    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4094854450140199873">Multiple award winning, #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Neil Gaiman returns to dazzle, captivate, haunt, and entertain with this third collection of short fiction following <i>Smoke and Mirrors</i> and <i>Fragile Things</i>--which includes a never-before published <i>American Gods</i> story, "Black Dog," written exclusively for this volume.<br/><br/>In this new anthology, Neil Gaiman pierces the ve</span>
  <span id="freeText4094854450140199873" style="display:none">Multiple award winning, #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author Neil Gaiman returns to dazzle, captivate, haunt, and entertain with this third collection of short fiction following <i>Smoke and Mirrors</i> and <i>Fragile Things</i>--which includes a never-before published <i>American Gods</i> story, "Black Dog," written exclusively for this volume.<br /><br />In this new anthology, Neil Gaiman pierces the veil of reality to reveal the enigmatic, shadowy world that lies beneath. <i>Trigger Warning</i> includes previously published pieces of short fiction--stories, verse, and a very special <i>Doctor Who</i> story that was written for the fiftieth anniversary of the beloved series in 2013--as well "Black Dog," a new tale that revisits the world of <i>American Gods</i>, exclusive to this collection.<br /><br /><i>Trigger Warning</i> explores the masks we all wear and the people we are beneath them to reveal our vulnerabilities and our truest selves. Here is a rich cornucopia of horror and ghosts stories, science fiction and fairy tales, fabulism and poetry that explore the realm of experience and emotion. In "Adventure Story"--a thematic companion to <i>The Ocean at the End of the Lane</i>--Gaiman ponders death and the way people take their stories with them when they die. His social media experience "A Calendar of Tales" are short takes inspired by replies to fan tweets about the months of the year--stories of pirates and the March winds, an igloo made of books, and a Mother's Day card that portends disturbances in the universe. Gaiman offers his own ingenious spin on <i>Sherlock Holmes</i> in his award-nominated mystery tale "The Case of Death and Honey". And "Click-Clack the Rattlebag" explains the creaks and clatter we hear when we're all alone in the darkness.<br /><br />A sophisticated writer whose creative genius is unparalleled, Gaiman entrances with his literary alchemy, transporting us deep into the realm of imagination, where the fantastical becomes real and the everyday incandescent. Full of wonder and terror, surprises and amusements, <i>Trigger Warning</i> is a treasury of delights that engage the mind, stir the heart, and shake the soul from one of the most unique and popular literary artists of our day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4094854450140199873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_37762389').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_37762389').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_37762389').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/456898-would-you-anyone-recommend-this-book-to">Would you [anyone] recommend this book to someone who hasn&#39;t previously read Doctor Who or Sherlock? Are the pieces actually stand-alone?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_456898'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F22522808-trigger-warning">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/456898-would-you-anyone-recommend-this-book-to">5 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/456898-would-you-anyone-recommend-this-book-to">See all 3 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/60461062-quern"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1476173867i/60461062._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/60461062-quern">Quern</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The stories don't rely on any particular information from Doctor Who or Sherlock Holmes, but some familiarity with the characters would increase your <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The stories don't rely on any particular information from Doctor Who or Sherlock Holmes, but some familiarity with the characters would increase your enjoyment of these stories (as you would be able to see how Gaiman has re-interpreted the characters and put his own spin on the themes), but it is not essential to understanding or enjoying them.<br /><br />Keep in mind that this is a book of short stories, so it is only two of them in the collection that mention these characters.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1215904145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1215904145" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1215904145?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1215904145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9313773090857329635"><blockquote>
  <b> The monsters in our cupboards and our minds are always there in the darkness, like mold beneath the floorboards and behind the wallpaper, and there is so much darkness, an inexhaustible supply of darkness. The universe is amply supplied with night.</b>
</blockquote>There is a diversity of material in Neil Gaiman’s third and latest collection of short fiction, <i>Trigger Warning</i>. It is a potpourri of twenty four pieces, if we take as a single piece the entry called <i>A Calendar of Tales</i>, which, itself, holds a doz</span>
  <span id="freeText9313773090857329635" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b> The monsters in our cupboards and our minds are always there in the darkness, like mold beneath the floorboards and behind the wallpaper, and there is so much darkness, an inexhaustible supply of darkness. The universe is amply supplied with night.</b>
</blockquote>There is a diversity of material in Neil Gaiman’s third and latest collection of short fiction, <i>Trigger Warning</i>. It is a potpourri of twenty four pieces, if we take as a single piece the entry called <i>A Calendar of Tales</i>, which, itself, holds a dozen. They are not all, despite the collection title, dark or frightening. He brings in some familiar names, David Bowie, Sherlock Holmes, Doctor Who, Maleficent, Snow White, a traveler from other Gaiman writings, Shadow Moon, twists endings into satisfactory curls for the most part, wanders far afield in setting and content, well, within the UK anyway, tosses in a few poems for good measure, and even offers up a few chuckles. He is fond not only of science fiction as a source, but of Scottish and Irish legends as well. If you are not smitten with the story you are reading at a given moment, not to worry, there is another close behind that is certain to satisfy. <blockquote>
  <blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418860402i/12924713.jpg" width="300" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Neil Gaiman</b> Photo by Kimberly Butler – on Harper Collins site</blockquote>
</blockquote>Gaiman is overt in noting the absence of connective tissue among the tales. But there are some themes that pop up a time or three. Living things interred in walls, whether after they had expired or not. A bit of time travelling. Fairy tales are fractured. Favorite writers are admired. <br><br>In the introduction, Gaiman tells us a bit about the origins of each of the 24, a nifty item to check back on after one has read them all. Some of the material has been developed for other media. I added a link at bottom to a more-than-text offering re the Calendar of Tales, for one.<br><br>Overall I found <i>Trigger Warning</i> is a pretty good survey of Gaiman’s impressive range. He seems able to realize the dreams of the alchemists by transforming what seems every experience he has and every notion that crosses his interior crawl into gold. And some of the stories here are glittery indeed. <br><br>I quite enjoyed the collection. The uplift of the best more than made up for the downdraft of the lesser. If you enjoy fantasy, with a good dollop of horror, you could definitely give it a shot. <br><br>==============================<b>THE STORIES</b><br><br>1 – <i>Making a Chair</i> – a poem about the writing process. <br><br>2 – <i>A Lunar Labyrinth</i> – a tribute to Gene Wolfe – a traveler who enjoys roadside oddities is brought to a maze that is brought into a form of darkness by the full moon.<br>Here is a link to a site that will clue you in on <a href="http://www.roadsideamerica.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">roadside oddities</a> in the USA. There is a book on such things for the other side of the pond, but I did not find a comparable link<br><br>3 – <i>The Thing about Cassandra</i> – An imaginary connection becomes real, with a delicious twist<br><br>4 – <i>Down to a Sunless Sea</i> – an abominable feast, but with some just desserts<br><br>5 – <i>The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountain</i> - A not wholly human dwarf engages a local man to lead him to a cave reputed to be filled with tainted gold – I could not get the image of Peter Dinklage as Tyrion Lannister out of my tiny mind while immersed in this one. Sometimes the truth hurts. <br><br>6 – <i>My Last Landlady</i> – the rent is definitely too damn high<br><br>7 – <i>Adventure Story</i> – a bit of fun guaranteed to make you smile<br><br>8 – <i>Orange</i> – A teen who thinks she’s all that may indeed be – another smile-worthy item<br><br>9 – <i>A Calendar of Tales</i> – I won’t go into each – the collection was written from ideas received on-line. I found it a mixed bag, with March (Mom has a big secret), August ( a tale of fire and foolishness), September (a magic ring with the quality of a bad penny), October (a sweet tale, involving a Jinni), and December (a hopeful time-travel piece) my favorites<br><br>10 – <i>The Case of Death and Honey</i> – a fantastical tale in which a certain Baker Street resident takes on the mystery of death itself<br><br>11 - <i>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury</i> – a tribute to Gaiman’s mentor<br><br>12 – <i>Jerusalem</i> – on one of the dangers of visiting the city<br><br>13 – <i>Click-clack the Rattlebag</i> – stories can be scary, regardless of the age of the teller<br><br>14 – <i>An Invocation of Incuriousity</i> – a time-travel piece – don’t touch the settings<br><br>15 – <i>And Weep, Like Alexander</i> – one possible reason why we do not have some of the futuristic inventions we expected long ago – cute, not scary<br><br>16 – <i>Nothing O’Clock</i> – a Doctor Who tale with a timely solution<br><br>17 – <i>Diamonds and Pearls: A Fairy Tale</i> – a fable with a moral<br><br>18 – <i>The Return of the Thin White Duke</i> – the completion of a story begun and abandoned while back for a magazine project on Bowie<br><br>19 – <i>Feminine Endings</i> – beware of street statue-performers<br><br>20 – <i>Observing the Formalities</i> – Maleficent as narrator of a poem about proper forms<br><br>21 – <i>The Sleeper and the Spindle</i> – A fairy tale with a nice twist<br><br>22 – <i>Witch Work</i> – a poem on the limits of witchy magic<br><br>23 – <i>In Relig Odhrain</i> – a poem on a saint who suffered an awful demise<br><br>24 – <i>Black Dog</i> – Shadow Moon stops in an ancient pub and is drawn into some serious darkness, scary fun.<br><br>Review posted – 3/20/15<br><br>Publication date – 2/3/2015<br><br>This review has also been posted at Cootsreviews.com<br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF</b><br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="http://www.neilgaiman.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a>, <a href="https://twitter.com/neilhimself" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, <a href="http://neil-gaiman.tumblr.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> and <a href="https://www.facebook.com/neilgaiman" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">FB</a> pages<br><br>Here is a link to his separate <a href="http://journal.neilgaiman.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br><br>For a full-on media-rich offering the <i>Calendar of Tales</i> piece in <i>Trigger Warning</i> can be seen <a href="http://www.acalendaroftales.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a><br><br>Harper has an on-line <a href="http://645e533e2058e72657e9-f9758a43fb7c33cc8adda0fd36101899.r45.cf2.rackcdn.com/reading-guides/RG-9780062330260.pdf" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">reading guide</a><br><br><b>Other Gaiman books</b> I have reviewed<br>-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1657101645" rel="nofollow noopener">The View from the Cheap Seats</a><br>-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/437207122" rel="nofollow noopener">The Graveyard Book</a><br>-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/693708734" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ocean at the End of the Lane</a><br>-----<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/34630914" rel="nofollow noopener">Stardust</a></span>

<div id="review_1336039670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1336039670" />
    <a title="Snotchocheez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1899836-snotchocheez"><img alt="Snotchocheez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510561146p2/1899836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1336039670?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snotchocheez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snotchocheez" href="/user/show/1899836-snotchocheez">Snotchocheez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">die-hard Gaiman fans with time on their hands (maybe)</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1336039670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4291667383997837944">Wow, I'm certainly in the minority on this one. (Or maybe not. Once the dust has settled and adoring Gaiman fans are finished slobbering over this truly uninspired collection of "short fictions and disturbances"...{read: cast-off ideas and random vanity-noodling}, I think that 3.94 cume might come crashing down). <br/><br/>(Or maybe I'm just a rock-hurling philistine. But, no, I really liked <i> American Gods</i>, I adored <i> The Ocean at the End of the Lane</i>, ditto <i> Coraline</i> and <i> Neverwhere</i>. Ok, not a die-hard fan</span>
  <span id="freeText4291667383997837944" style="display:none">Wow, I'm certainly in the minority on this one. (Or maybe not. Once the dust has settled and adoring Gaiman fans are finished slobbering over this truly uninspired collection of "short fictions and disturbances"...{read: cast-off ideas and random vanity-noodling}, I think that 3.94 cume might come crashing down). <br /><br />(Or maybe I'm just a rock-hurling philistine. But, no, I really liked <i> American Gods</i>, I adored <i> The Ocean at the End of the Lane</i>, ditto <i> Coraline</i> and <i> Neverwhere</i>. Ok, not a die-hard fan here, but I sure appreciate his vivid imagination, if not his "literary alchemy" {huh? hyperbolize much, blurb writers?}) <br /><br />All I can say is, of this previously-published collection of 24 entries (including 4 lackluster poems), <i> maybe</i> three of them seemed remotely worthwhile. (In baseball parlance, 3 for 24 is a .125 batting average, hardly a collection to drool over). <br /><br />I should have been leery with the inordinate amount of time Gaiman used in the introduction to preface <i> Trigger Warning</i>, almost like a used car salesman trumping up the virtues of a shiny retread, knowing full well that underneath the fresh wax job is an engine just waiting to throw a rod. Seriously, if it weren't for the strength of the very last tale, "Black Dog" (not coincidentally, the longest offering, and really the only one with a consistently enjoyable plot arc, somewhat tied to the <i> American Gods</i> metaverse) this probably would've gotten one star from me. Most everything here (except the last story, and, perhaps, "Nothing O'Clock" {an episode of "Doctor Who" Gaiman penned}) needs to be returned to the idea box, and either expanded upon, or scrapped.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4291667383997837944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1962974989" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1962974989" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1962974989?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781472217684" href="/book/show/23628916-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=darkness-horror-gothic">darkness-horror-gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1962974989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15608805751439346941">Gaiman has written so many weird and wonderful things over the years. I find his talent truly remarkable, especially the way he can dip in and out of different genres. He does not restrict himself to one style, but plays around with words and stories like a true master. He is one of the most multi-talented writers alive today. <br/><br/>And in here there is a collection of very diverse pieces. We have fantasy and horror. We have those drawn from myths and the writings of other authors. My particular favou</span>
  <span id="freeText15608805751439346941" style="display:none">Gaiman has written so many weird and wonderful things over the years. I find his talent truly remarkable, especially the way he can dip in and out of different genres. He does not restrict himself to one style, but plays around with words and stories like a true master. He is one of the most multi-talented writers alive today. <br /><br />And in here there is a collection of very diverse pieces. We have fantasy and horror. We have those drawn from myths and the writings of other authors. My particular favourite was <i>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury.</i> It’s more of a recognition piece than an actual story. Gaiman pays homage to a man who influenced him artistically and intellectually; he even sent the work to Bradbury in hospital shortly before he died, and he responded with a thank you video. It’s a touching story, but it felt at odds with some of the others in here. <br /><br />As far as typical short story collections go, this doesn’t quite work. Only in the sense that short story collections are supposed to be a collection of similar stories, at least in terms of theme and purpose, successful ones speak to each other as you progress through. I’m of course thinking about the writing of Alice Munro and James Joyce here, and other greats of the short story form. However, this doesn’t quite do the same thing. This isn’t new work by Gaiman, as his recent collection of stories <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30831912-norse-mythology?ac=1&amp;from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Norse Mythology</a> is. Instead, short stories he has written over the years (some as many as seven years apart) are published here altogether for the first time. It’s completely random.<br /><br />They are all brought together by this very loose idea of a “trigger warning.” It’s an idea that there will be a trigger within the writing, a glimpse of something unusual or uncanny that reveals the unseen. It’s an immediate shift of tone. Gaiman defines it in the introduction: <br /><br /><i>"There are little things that upset us. That’s not quite what we’re talking about here, tough. I’m thinking about those images or words or ideas that drop like trapdoors beneath us, throwing us out of our safe, sane world into a place much more dark and less welcoming. Our hearts skip a ratatat drumbeat into our chests, and we fight for breath. Blood retreats from our faces and our fingers, leaving us pale and gasping and shocked. And what we learn about ourselves in those moments, where the trigger has been squeezed, is this: the past is not dead."</i><br /><br />Certainly, such a descriptor fits some of the stories perfectly, and in some cases I could sense the exact line or phrase: it was blatant. In other cases, there was no semblance of one. The Bradbury story, though in itself a fantastic piece of writing, does not have one. I can only conclude that such a thing was used as an attempt to bring unrelated stories together and market them as a collection of writing. So I found this rather difficult to review. Most of the short stories in here are really good pieces of writing, Gaiman at his best, though they don’t all fit the model the book is trying to prescribe. Think of it this way: you have a bunch of lovely ingredients and each in their own right are enjoyable, but when thrown together the result is a big mess. <br /><br />However, I can’t overlook those original ingredients. They don’t work together, but on their own they are still good; thus, I only recommend this to loyal fans of the author, those that love his writing and are perhaps willing to overlook some of the issues here if it means reading more of the said writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15608805751439346941" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1962974989">

<div id="review_1408931616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1408931616" />
    <a title="Lyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn"><img alt="Lyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495541962p2/5253785.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1408931616?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyn" href="/user/show/5253785-lyn">Lyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1408931616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10182032261709480888">I have opined before that Neil Gaiman is the literary heir to Ray Bradbury’s rich legacy, being of mind to celebrate imagination whilst acting as a guide to the shadowy places in the calliope we call life.<br/><br/>Trigger Warning is Gailman’s 2015 collection of shorter work and much of it is in the spirit of Bradbury but with Gailman’s special voice. Twenty-three separate pieces are presented to delight those readers accustomed to visiting that country between dusk and shadow frequented by Gailman and Br</span>
  <span id="freeText10182032261709480888" style="display:none">I have opined before that Neil Gaiman is the literary heir to Ray Bradbury’s rich legacy, being of mind to celebrate imagination whilst acting as a guide to the shadowy places in the calliope we call life.<br><br>Trigger Warning is Gailman’s 2015 collection of shorter work and much of it is in the spirit of Bradbury but with Gailman’s special voice. Twenty-three separate pieces are presented to delight those readers accustomed to visiting that country between dusk and shadow frequented by Gailman and Bradbury. Gailman also pays tribute to Jack Vance with a visit to the dying earth, “The Case of Death and Honey” a Sherlock and Mycroft Holmes story, “Nothing O’Clock” a Doctor Who short work, several reconstructed fairy tales, and “Black Dog” a special appearance by Shadow Moon of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4407.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a> fame.<br><br>My favorite (made me smile) is of course “The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury”. Something that can never happen.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1507037290i/24075910.jpg" width="300" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10182032261709480888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2177750998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177750998" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177750998?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177750998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5206729910802524066"><b>I'm generally not a huge fan of short stories and this book was no exception. </b><br/><br/>By far, my favorite short story was <b>Click-Clack the Rattlebag</b> that was brilliant and eerie and just everything wonderful. There were some other spooky stories (i.e. <b>The Truth about Cassandra</b> or <b>Feminine Endings</b>) that I enjoyed but (as usual) I didn't like most of them AND only one of them was actually new. The rest are republished from other anthologies. Some were even published fully on their own before (i.e. a book).</span>
  <span id="freeText5206729910802524066" style="display:none"><b>I'm generally not a huge fan of short stories and this book was no exception. </b><br /><br />By far, my favorite short story was <b>Click-Clack the Rattlebag</b> that was brilliant and eerie and just everything wonderful. There were some other spooky stories (i.e. <b>The Truth about Cassandra</b> or <b>Feminine Endings</b>) that I enjoyed but (as usual) I didn't like most of them AND only one of them was actually new. The rest are republished from other anthologies. Some were even published fully on their own before (i.e. a book). <br /><br />And of course, because this is Neil Gaiman, <b>he throws in a bunch of weird sex.</b> Sigh.<br /><br />Without further ado:<br /><br /><b>Introduction</b> - Felt like he was trying to justify these short stories to get people to read them. <br /><br /><b>Making A Chair</b> - A poetic comparison between a chair and the writing process. Not particularly interesting. <br /><br /><b>A Lunar Labyrinth</b> - A traveler, a maze and the darkness of the full moon. There's references to Gene Wolfe but that went over my head.<br /><br /><b>The Thing About Cassandra</b> - Quite good! An imaginary girlfriend drops back into the main character's life - just as his career reaches a pinnacle. The twist ending had me setting down this book and pondering how crazy it was.<br /><br /><b>Down To A Sunless Sea</b> - A woman loses her son to the sea. An encounter years later reveals a cruel and terrible fate. <br /><br /><b>The Truth Is A Cave In The Black Mountains</b> - THIS DOES NOT COUNT - it was published once in Stories (2010) and again as a fully illustrated short story (2014). A man, a dwarf, a cursed cavern and a burning desire for revenge.<br /><br /><b>My Last Landlady</b> - The renter reflects on his quirky past landlady. The landlady makes short work of her renters and despite being gone they still linger...<br /><br /><b>Adventure Story</b> - An older woman refers to the most mundane aspects as an adventure and the craziest moments ad normal reality. This one was actually fun - exactly how I aspire to live my life.<br /><br /><b>Orange</b> - orange hair dye + ancient goddess =/= great combination. His older sister rubs some orange goop into her skin in an effort to become tanner, turns out that allowed the goddess to take over. Told only through the answers of a questionnaire form - quirky and interesting. <br /><br /><b>A Calendar Of Tales</b> - Each month told its own story. Most were uninteresting. I feel like this should have been longer than death.<br /><br /><b>The Case Of Death And Honey</b> - A Sherlock themed story - probably the longest and most boring I've read. Sherlock's even bored in the story (and not in the fun <i>BORED</i> of BBC's version, more like he's literally raising bees.)<br /><br /><b>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury</b> - Tribute to a mentor. I never read much of Ray Bradbury, thus this was all lost on me. <br /><br /><b>Jerusalem</b> - A brief look into the madness that comes with extreme devotion. A woman pilgrimages to the holy city only to go crazy once she gets there.<br /><br /><b>Click-Clack The Rattlebag</b> - Brilliant and shockingly so. This made the whole book worth the read. Seriously. This could be a great book on its own. A teenager is babysitting his girlfriend's little brother and makes the mistake of asking the kid for a scary story. That kid delivered.<br /><br /><b>An Invocation Of Incuriosity</b> - A terrible father has no qualms regarding his youngest son's life and inheritance. Felt vaguely cinderella-ish with the way the son had to serve the other family despite being the true heir. <br /><br /><b>And Weep, Like Alexander</b> - One man stands in the way of complete and terrible inventions. His sole job - unmake everything that leads outside of the normal realm of invention. Anything annoying or overpowering (i.e. jetpacks) were unmade by him.<br /><br /><b>Nothing O'Clock</b> - My first Dr Who book. The characters seemed a smidge off from the episodes but this was an intriguing issue.<br /><br /><b>Diamonds And Pearls: A Fairy Tale</b> - Modern fairy tale(ish) kind of like the one where the good girl is nice to a fairy and every time she speaks jewels fall out. But with cocaine and hookers. About as bad as you think it would be.<br /><br /><b>The Return Of The Thin White Duke</b> - David Bowie themed fan fiction (in Gaiman's words). It's strange.<br /><br /><b>Feminine Endings</b> - Creepy one about a living statue that set his eyes on one particular girl. As usual with Gaiman, it got weirdly sexual and included panty-inspections.<br /><br /><b>Observing The Formalities</b> - Narrated poem. Not memorable.<br /><br /><b>The Sleeper And The Spindle</b> - THIS DOES NOT COUNT - it was published as a fully illustrated short story (2014)<br /><br /><b>Witch Work</b> - Poem on witch magic<br /><br /><b>In Relig Odhráin</b> - poem about saint and church.<br /><br /><b>Black Dog</b> - THIS WAS LITERALLY THE ONLY NEW ONE. It's an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30165203.American_Gods__American_Gods___1_" title="American Gods (American Gods, #1) by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">American Gods</a> short story. Marginally interesting but I haven't read American Gods before picking this up, thus it was somewhat lost on me.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5206729910802524066" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1164904524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1164904524" />
    <a title="Jessica Woodbury" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4271946-jessica-woodbury"><img alt="Jessica Woodbury" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415105097p2/4271946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1164904524?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Woodbury" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Woodbury" href="/user/show/4271946-jessica-woodbury">Jessica Woodbury</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062330291" href="/book/show/22500611-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=arc-provided-by-publisher">arc-provided-by-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4271946-jessica-woodbury?shelf=story-collection">story-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1164904524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer156284170327392041">I prefer Gaiman's novel-length work, but you do get something in this collection you don't get in longform: his huge range and vast depths of creativity. Most readers will probably only connect with a few pieces here, but it's worth it to read the ones you don't dig as much because they're just so different and so inventive and it's hard to believe they all came from one brain.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1260650182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1260650182" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1260650182?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=short-story-collections">short-story-collections</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1260650182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14646577426076765260"><b>I built an igloo out of books in my backyard.<br/><br/>I slept in my igloo made of books. I was getting hungry. I made a hole in the floor, lowered a fishing line and waited until something bit. I pulled it up: a fish made of books - green covered vintage Penguin detective stories. I ate it raw, fearing a fire in my igloo.<br/><br/>When I went outside I observed that someone had covered the whole world with books: pale-covered books, all shades of white and blue and purple. I wandered the ice floes of books.<br/><br/>I saw s</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14646577426076765260" style="display:none"><b>I built an igloo out of books in my backyard.<br /><br />I slept in my igloo made of books. I was getting hungry. I made a hole in the floor, lowered a fishing line and waited until something bit. I pulled it up: a fish made of books - green covered vintage Penguin detective stories. I ate it raw, fearing a fire in my igloo.<br /><br />When I went outside I observed that someone had covered the whole world with books: pale-covered books, all shades of white and blue and purple. I wandered the ice floes of books.<br /><br />I saw someone who looked like my wife out there on the ice. She was making a glacier of autobiographies.<br /><br />"I thought you left me," I said to her. "I thought you left me alone."<br /><br />She said nothing, and I realized she was only a shadow of a shadow.</b>*<br /><br /><br /><br />This is a fine collection of short fiction and poetry. I honestly liked this more than any of Gaiman's novels I've read so far, but then, I'm a huge fan of short stories. Even the few tales here that I wasn't too fond of were engaging and well written. <br /><br />There are too many wonders in these pages to count them all. <br /><br />One of my favorites was <b>
  <i>The Sleeper and the Spindle</i>
</b> in which a queen blows off her impending nuptials to rescue a sleeping beauty. (Good for her! Handsome Princes are boring and not nearly as good in bed as they think they are!)<br /><br /> I also liked <b>
  <i>"And Weep Like Alexander,"</i>
</b> which answers once and for all the question of "Why don't we have personal jet-packs by now?" <br /><br />My absolute favorite, though, was the poignant <b>
  <i>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury.</i>
</b> I never stopped to think that when you have Alzheimer's, you not only forget everyone you love, but your favorite books as well.<br /><br />*from <b>
  <i>A Calendar of Tales</i>
</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14646577426076765260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1244306418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244306418" />
    <a title="Char " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6581119-char"><img alt="Char " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415394568p2/6581119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1244306418?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Char " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Char " href="/user/show/6581119-char">Char </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780062373625" href="/book/show/22500627-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6581119-char?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244306418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer972945652802251065"><b>Trigger Warning by Neil Gaiman (narrated by Neil Gaiman)</b> "The Man Who Remembered Ray Bradbury"was an outstanding story! It made  me think of my favorite short story by James Everington titled "A Writer's Words". (Which is included in his collection The Other Room. )It also deepened my sadness about Terry Pratchett.  I can only imagine what it's like for a man of words to start losing those words. Just the thought of it makes me sad and gives me goosebumps. 5 big fat stars for this tale!<br/> <br/>Unfortun</span>
  <span id="freeText972945652802251065" style="display:none"><b>Trigger Warning by Neil Gaiman (narrated by Neil Gaiman)</b> "The Man Who Remembered Ray Bradbury"was an outstanding story! It made  me think of my favorite short story by James Everington titled "A Writer's Words". (Which is included in his collection The Other Room. )It also deepened my sadness about Terry Pratchett.  I can only imagine what it's like for a man of words to start losing those words. Just the thought of it makes me sad and gives me goosebumps. 5 big fat stars for this tale!<br /> <br />Unfortunately, I hated the rest of this audio book.  So much so that I'm throwing in the towel at 85%. I am going to go ahead and rate it even though I don't usually rate my DNFs. Since I made it through 85%, I feel that I am sufficiently qualified to rate it and I do so at 2.5 stars. If it weren't for the Ray Bradbury story I would probably have given this a one star, instead.<br /> <br />I know, I know-it's Neil Gaiman. The stories were well written, of course, but perhaps it's the author himself reading the stories that I don't like? I just found my mind wandering almost the entire time I was listening. I've listened to audiobooks of short stories before and have liked them, so I'm not sure why this one didn't work. Maybe the stories themselves were just boring? It's most likely some combination of the two. <br /> <br />In any case, I'm glad to be done with this audio book, since I found myself dreading it every time I went to resume listening. I think it's obvious at this point that I don't recommend this collection. But if you see it in the library or bookstore, pick it up and quickly read "The Man Who Remembered Ray Bradbury" and then put it back down and leave. </span>
  <a data-text-id="972945652802251065" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1175777604" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175777604" />
    <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede"><img alt="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487436758p2/1379514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175777604?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede" href="/user/show/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede">Magdalena aka A Bookaholic Swede</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1379514-magdalena-aka-a-bookaholic-swede?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175777604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8924458427273137565"><strong>Trigger Warning</strong> is a collection of short stories and some poems by <strong>Neil Gaiman</strong>. What I like about collections like this one is that they usually have something for us all. Not everything is to one's liking, but if you are lucky most are. And, <strong>Trigger Warning</strong> is mostly, in my opinion, a very good collection of stories. Of course, some are better than the others and I think personally I liked the ones that were a bit longer. The "bad" thing with collections like this is they are sometimes hard to </span>
  <span id="freeText8924458427273137565" style="display:none"><strong>Trigger Warning</strong> is a collection of short stories and some poems by <strong>Neil Gaiman</strong>. What I like about collections like this one is that they usually have something for us all. Not everything is to one's liking, but if you are lucky most are. And, <strong>Trigger Warning</strong> is mostly, in my opinion, a very good collection of stories. Of course, some are better than the others and I think personally I liked the ones that were a bit longer. The "bad" thing with collections like this is they are sometimes hard to put down because it so easy to just say to yourself "just one more story" they are short. And, then you happen to stumble over a Doctor Who story that isn't that short, but you have to read it because it is Doctor Who, even despite the fact that is an 11 Doctor story (Long story short, not my favorite Doctor).<br /><br />Anyway, instead of writing about every story in this collection will I mention some of my favorites like:<br /><br /><strong>The Truth Is a Cave in the Black Mountains</strong>, one of the longest stories in this book and a very intriguing to read.<br /><br /><strong>Orange</strong>, the kind of story that grows on you. I found questionnaire format of the story odd in the beginning, but then I started to like it.<br /><br /><strong>The Case of Death and Honey</strong>, a Sherlock Holmes story, I have read it before in another collection, but I read it again since it was a while ago. One of the best Sherlock Holmes short stories I have ever read and I have a feeling I like it even better than the first time I read it.<br /><br /><strong>Jerusalem</strong>, what I enjoyed with this story was that I had no idea that Jerusalem Syndrome was a thing and I really enjoyed the wonderful twist in the story. Would I dare travel to Jerusalem in the future?<br /><br /><strong>Click-Clack the Rattlebag</strong>, the only story in this collection that actually was a bit scary. I mean I wasn't scared when I read it but reading this when you are alone in a house and hearing sounds in the attic would probably not be that nice.<br /><br /><strong>"And Weep, Like Alexander"</strong>, oh that ending, marvelous! A charming and funny story.<br /><br /><strong>Nothing O´Clock</strong>, the Doctor Who story and as I wrote above not my favorite Doctor but Gaiman can write stories so good that I enjoyed this one despite that. And last but not the least,<br /><br /><strong>The Sleeper and the Spindle</strong>, for some reason I thought the title was the Sleeper and the Spider. I think sometimes your mind plays tricks on you. Anyway, Spindle makes much more sense and I liked this once upon a time story very much.<br /><br />There are several other good stories, but these are some that I appreciated.<br /><br /><em>Thanks to William Morrow and Edelweiss for providing me with a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review!</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="8924458427273137565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7452661716356318869" style="display:none">I have enjoyed this collection of stories. I think this winter has been a perfect time to read them too. I feel almost like the crinkle and crackle under my feet like leaves as I read them. Or I am in my dark room with the reading light on under a mound of covers in the cold winter night. I found this collection did what I needed it too. I feel like Neil is always opening new doors in my head to unknown destinations in the universe I never went to. Its strange; I usually only read creepy horror writers for short stories. I like Stephen King, Edgar Allen Poe and Neil Gaiman short stories. Otherwise I don't read much of it. So, this was my cup of tea.<br /><br />Enjoy</span>

<div id="review_1217331011" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217331011" />
    <a title="MLE  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2761976-mle"><img alt="MLE  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457529294p2/2761976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217331011?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MLE  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="MLE  " href="/user/show/2761976-mle">MLE  </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062330291" href="/book/show/22500611-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2761976-mle?shelf=ghost-and-horror">ghost-and-horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217331011" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer539041489130713614">A fantastic collection of short stories and poems by my favorite living author. While I didn't love every story in this collection there were ones that were just perfect. <br/><br/>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury was powerful, and especially moving considering his friendship with Terry Pratchett. A beautiful, and haunting reflection on the power of words, of ideas, of books, and of stories. A story that addressed some of my personal biggest fears.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427684457i/14306580.jpg' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Click-Clack the Rattlebag was just the kind of creeping, an</span>
  <span id="freeText539041489130713614" style="display:none">A fantastic collection of short stories and poems by my favorite living author. While I didn't love every story in this collection there were ones that were just perfect. <br><br>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury was powerful, and especially moving considering his friendship with Terry Pratchett. A beautiful, and haunting reflection on the power of words, of ideas, of books, and of stories. A story that addressed some of my personal biggest fears.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427684457i/14306580.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Click-Clack the Rattlebag was just the kind of creeping, and atmospheric horror story I like. Scary, and dark without being obvious and silly. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428074852i/14359299._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Nothing O'clock was the perfect fusion of my favorite author and one of my favorite shows. Exactly how much love the author has for Doctor Who shines in these pages. His grasp of Amy and the Eleventh Doctor was perfect, and I could see the story playing out in my head just like an episode of the show. The balance of humor, and darkness was just right. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428074852i/14359300.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The fairy tale re-imaginings were all different, but each drew on the feel of the original tales. Each dark, and more than a bit gruesome in their own way. No traditional happy endings, or Princes to the rescue here. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428074852i/14359301._SY540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Black Dog was an excellent addition to American Gods universe. I don't think that you have to have read American Gods before you read this. It might give you a little more context, and it might be helpful to know <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that Shadow isn't precisely all human <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his father is Odin <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I don't think it's vital to understanding the story either. Just know that after some difficulties Shadow has been traveling or wandering in Europe. I love the history, and mythology in this story. It only makes me long for more.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1428074852i/14359302.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall a good, darker selection of Neil Gaiman stories. The kind of horror that sneaks up on you. The kind built from suggestion, atmosphere, and character and not copious amounts of blood and gore. In short my favorite kind of horror. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415670414i/11827505._SX540_.jpg" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

And then, I think about the need to help others, and how we mask ourselves to do it, and how unmasking makes us vulnerable . . .<br />We are all wearing masks. That is what makes us interesting. <div id="review_2004399998" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004399998" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004399998?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062330291" href="/book/show/22500611-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=2017-library-love-challenge">2017-library-love-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=tbr-2017">tbr-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004399998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3702344981691279281">I meant to just read this book when I was on my trip to Ecuador next week, but decided to finish it now since my library has a bunch of books I put on hold come up for me to borrow. If I can finish a few others one before Monday I am going to be happy.<br/><br/>Back to this collection. Meh. And you also get an eyeroll. <br/><br/>Gaiman begins this going into how he became fascinated by "trigger warnings" and how they morphed from being a warning you saw onto the internet to them being used by professors in colleges</span>
  <span id="freeText3702344981691279281" style="display:none">I meant to just read this book when I was on my trip to Ecuador next week, but decided to finish it now since my library has a bunch of books I put on hold come up for me to borrow. If I can finish a few others one before Monday I am going to be happy.<br /><br />Back to this collection. Meh. And you also get an eyeroll. <br /><br />Gaiman begins this going into how he became fascinated by "trigger warnings" and how they morphed from being a warning you saw onto the internet to them being used by professors in colleges are using this now for warnings to their students before they read a book they fear may upset them. Then he does a huge condescending take about how as adults we should read without any warnings besides knowing what you read is at your own risk. <br /><br />First, many reviewers like myself use trigger warnings in order to warn potential readers about something that may upset them. For me, I always warn other reviewers about a rape scene being depicted in the book. Since every 98 seconds someone is raped in the United States, I feel like for a lot of us out there, we have experienced that first hand, we don't want to read about it if we have the option to skip over it. Heck, people won't watch movies that show an animal being hurt/killed and I don't mock people for feeling that way. <br /><br />Second, there seems to be two things going on in his introduction. People using trigger warnings on the internet to warn someone about a picture or image that would be hard to see I think is always a good thing. I do agree that college is a time for learning and to stretch yourself. Heck, I didn't even know you could refuse to read a book or material because it upset you. Do I think that things like that have gotten a little out of hand? Yes, possibly. But I think the intentions behind it are good. <br /><br />Third, you don't have to be condescending about what other people do and don't read. And also if you are going to act as if your stories in your collection are going to be so dark and so scary that you have to warn readers you better damn well bring it. He did not. This was a mediocre collection at best. I only liked/loved two stories and wish that they were available to buy solo. I refuse to buy this book just to have those two stories. <br /><br />"Making a Chair" (1 star)-I called this, great Neil Gaiman is writing another poem that I can just skip right over. I am not a fan of his poems. My streak continues alive.<br /><br />"A Lunar Labyrinth" (2 stars)-This was confusing. I also got really bored. I think that main narrator was a bad person and or possibly a murder. I have no idea. I was mildly intrigued by the idea of a labyrinth that you could walk during a full moon. The images that it evoked in my mind while reading were more interesting than actually finishing this story.<br /><br />"The Thing About Cassandra" (1 star)-Nope. I don't even want to get into this whole thing besides I found it to be a waste of time. <br /><br />"Down to a Sunless Sea" (1 star)-I don't know. I can't even say something pithy. It didn't move me beyond wanting to get to the next story so I could be done with this one. At least it was fairly short. It only ended up being like three electronic pages. <br /><br />"The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountains..."(4 stars)-This one was actually interesting. I think that it could have been a bit longer since I found myself very fascinated by the main character who comes to call on a man named Calum MacInnes who can lead him to a cave full of gold. I did love the foreshadowing that Gaiman sets up in this story. And it's a long winding road but you start to realize why this little man was so intent on hiring Calum MacInnes. The ending was good. <br /><br />"My Last Landlady" (1 star)-It's not a poem, but is trying to be. Enough said.<br /><br />"Adventure Story" (1 star)-I still don't get the point of this story.<br /><br />"Orange" (3 stars)-I liked the whole idea that it was a story, but a subject's response to a questionnaire. I really wish that we could have seen the questions too though. I spent more time trying to guess what the questions were to make the answers work.<br /><br />"A Calendar of Tales" (3 stars)-You get 12 mini short stories that are pegged to the calendar. So you get a January Tale, February Tale, and so on. I imagine that these are the tales that were told by the months that came to life that are featured in one of Gaiman's other short story collections. Some were interesting, some were not.<br /><br />"The Case of Death and Honey" (1 star)-This is a Sherlock Holmes tale and it's a story within a story within an even stupider story. It didn't make any sense. The changing text size and fonts were hard to read and just helped make things worse.<br /><br />"The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury" (1 star)-Shrug. <br /><br />"Jerusalem"(3 stars)-This was an interesting story about a couple that travels to Jerusalem and the affect the place has on them. I wish this could have been longer or provided some more details here and there. <br /><br />"Click-Clack the Rattlebag" (3 stars)-The only semi-scary story in the whole book. <br /><br />"An Invocation of Incuriousity" (3 stars)-An interesting idea that intrigued me but then the story kind of fell apart for me. <br /><br />"And Weep, Like Alexander" (2 stars)-If I ever met the guy who is the uninventor in this story I would have probably have moved away from him cause he sounds really annoying.<br /><br />"Nothing O'Clock" (3 stars)-This is a Doctor Who short story. I honestly cannot even remember if this made it into the series or not since I have stopped watching that show (sorry it got ridiculous and boring and if it makes you dislike me, have at it) so it was nice to read a story starring Eleven (The Doctor) and Amy Pond. It really felt weird that it was in this collection though. And it definitely highlights my issues with The Doctor and his former companions that were not Rose or Donna. <br /><br />"Diamonds and Pearls: A Fairy Tale"(1 star)-This was short and weird. And not in a good way.<br /><br />"The Return of the Thin White Duke" (1 star)-I feel like I am missing out on some big idea that Gaiman was going for in most of his stories. I feel like mumbling the phrase "try hard" when I read most of these stories. <br /><br />"Feminine Endings" (2 stars)-Oh joy, we get to read about a stalker (possibly a living statue) that is judging a woman who watches him on her trips back and forth just enjoying her life. I don't give it 2 stars because of that. I give it 2 stars because it was boring and just lame. <br /><br />"Observing the Formalities" (2 stars)-I am just going to pretend this is the lead in to the next story and ignore it being some weird spoken poem sort of thing.<br /><br />"The Sleeper and the Spindle" (5 stars)-I really enjoyed this a whole lot. I could read about a kick ass Snow White all day. I wonder about any further adventures she is going to have. <br /><br />"Witch Work" (1 star)-Another poem. It's short.<br /><br />"In Relig Odhrain" (1 star)-A poem. <br /><br />"Black Dog" (5 stars)-We see what Shadow has been up to since we have read of him in "Monarch of the Glen". I loved it. It has callbacks to characters we know like Bast and references to Odin too. Due to Shadow and who he is (no spoilers) I liked how this was done. And honestly I was stunned by misdirection I got. I definitely did not see any of this coming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3702344981691279281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1488929995" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1488929995" />
    <a title="Paul Nelson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson"><img alt="Paul Nelson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434048386p2/7553206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1488929995?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul Nelson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul Nelson" href="/user/show/7553206-paul-nelson">Paul Nelson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=2016-books-read">2016-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7553206-paul-nelson?shelf=its-gaiman">its-gaiman</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1488929995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17169254015574116980"><i>
  <b>'I don’t understand parents. Honestly, I don’t think anybody ever does.'</b>
</i><br/><br/>Trigger Warning is a short story and poem collection by Neil Gaiman intent on finding those little pressure points that cause the most unease and arouse reflection, maybe even disturb you a mite.<br/><br/>There's some little gems here but first I'll explain why I like Gaimans wondrous prose and fascinating stories. He thoughtfully exploits the story twist and role reversal better than anyone but it's the little things that stick w</span>
  <span id="freeText17169254015574116980" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>'I don’t understand parents. Honestly, I don’t think anybody ever does.'</b>
</i><br /><br />Trigger Warning is a short story and poem collection by Neil Gaiman intent on finding those little pressure points that cause the most unease and arouse reflection, maybe even disturb you a mite.<br /><br />There's some little gems here but first I'll explain why I like Gaimans wondrous prose and fascinating stories. He thoughtfully exploits the story twist and role reversal better than anyone but it's the little things that stick with me, shown perfectly in <i>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury. </i><br /><br /><i>
  <b>'I went to the shelf and the dictionary was gone, just a dictionary-sized hole in my shelf to show where my dictionary wasn’t.'</b>
</i> <br /><br />Now that sentence probably wouldn't appear in most people's favourite quotes and to be fair it's easily passed and forgotten, but it stayed in the forefront of my mind as I listened to the audio. So much so that I spent 30 minutes desperately trying to find it in the kindle version. This perfectly shows the way Neil Gaiman thinks and writes, exploration of a mute fancy that no-one else would even consider wasting a second on, all in a sentence and that's why I love it.<br /><br />Gaiman travels far and wide in this collection, from the last of the Time Lords to Sherlock Holmes and honey bees, from the fancifully dark fairy tale to Shadow from American Gods traveling through my home region of the Peak District encountering ghosts and murder.<br /><br /><i>The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountains</i> is a haunting tale of travel and treasure, family and murder, darkness, revenge and regret, desire of the soul. A true delight and I will certainly revisit the illustrated version of this story.<br /><br /><i>
  <b> ‘The Misty Isle is not as other places. And the mist that surrounds it is not like other mists.’ </b>
</i><br /><br /><i>Nothing O'Clock</i> sees the return of the Doctor and a foe worthy of terror, what can only be described as strangeness beyond belief starts with a person wearing an animal mask buying a house for cash. It soon becomes wholesale as property everywhere is being bought for cash by people wearing animal makes and they want one thing, for you to ask them the time.<br /><br />Sherlock Holmes makes an appearance in <i>The Case of Death and Honey</i> as Mycroft breathes his last and case of research in a far off land into honey and a particular bee. <i>The Sleeper and the Spindle</i> is a delightful cross of fairy tales with Sleeping Beauty and Snow White and the seven dwarfs.<br /><br />There's far too many stories and favourites to mention them all but safe to say I enjoyed this immensely, Neil Gaiman is one of my favourite authors and an incredibly talented guy. The absolute perfect medium to pull back that thin veil between worlds and explore the darkness beyond. A simply masterful story teller.<br /><br />Just as captivating is Neil Gaiman himself talking about the stories and those little triggers, things that upset us, leave our heart beating overtime, shock, not gore but mind messing at its best.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>'What we read as adults should be read, I think, with no warnings or alerts beyond, perhaps: enter at your own risk.'</b>
</i><br /><br />Also posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/1321106/trigger-warning-by-neil-gaiman">http://paulnelson.booklikes.com/post/...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17169254015574116980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
