<div id="review_1207164675" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1207164675" />
    <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy"><img alt="Jenny (Reading Envy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455391853p2/68030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1207164675?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny (Reading Envy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny (Reading Envy)" href="/user/show/68030-jenny-reading-envy">Jenny (Reading Envy)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=read2015">read2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=sci-fi-fantasy">sci-fi-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68030-jenny-reading-envy?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1207164675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13696864924290098430">As usual with short story anthologies - some I was not interested in, some I loved. What I wish was less often - how many of these stories I'd read already, published in other compilations. I know it's an author's prerogative how they bundle and republish their work, but I'd prefer to be given new stories.<br/><br/>Don't skip the introductions. They put each story into context and one has a hint of a future novel (very exciting!)<br/><br/>My favorites:<br/><br/>-The Thing About Cassandra<br/><br/>-The Truth is a Cave in the Black Moun</span>
  <span id="freeText13696864924290098430" style="display:none">As usual with short story anthologies - some I was not interested in, some I loved. What I wish was less often - how many of these stories I'd read already, published in other compilations. I know it's an author's prerogative how they bundle and republish their work, but I'd prefer to be given new stories.<br /><br />Don't skip the introductions. They put each story into context and one has a hint of a future novel (very exciting!)<br /><br />My favorites:<br /><br />-The Thing About Cassandra<br /><br />-The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountains (recommended: the separate Audible production with the FourPlay String Quartet)<br /><br />-Black Dog<br /><i>It is important to note that depression is often referred to as the "black dog."</i><br /><br />-The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury - a lovely tribute to an author and more generally, ruminations on what happens to works once they're out there<br /><br />"I sometimes imagine I would like my ashes to be scattered in a library. But then the librarians would just have to come in early the next morning to sweep them up again."<br /><br />-In <i>Relig Odhráin</i> - largely because it was set on a tiny island that both the author and I adore. I would love to go back and read this story again while standing near this place.<br /><br />Stories I'd already read: <br />-Click-Clack the Rattlebag<br />-The Sleeper and the Spindle<br />-Feminine Endings<br /><br />ETA: This book was discussed on <a href="http://readingenvy.blogspot.com/2015/03/reading-envy-podcast-episode-024.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Episode 024 of the Reading Envy podast.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13696864924290098430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1724645742" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1724645742" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1724645742?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the strange, magical and wonderful (and Gaiman fans of course)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=short-story">short-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=anthology-collection">anthology-collection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43881851-ron?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1724645742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16541154284293465099"><b>Trigger Warning:</b> <i>a statement at the start of a piece of writing, video, etc., alerting the reader or viewer to the fact that it contains potentially distressing material (often used to introduce a description of such content).</i> Cool huh? Gaiman opens his book of short stories with why he decided on the book’s name, and then states, “What we read as adults should be read, I think, with no warnings or alerts beyond, perhaps: enter at your own risk”.<br/><br/>To me, that’s a challenge. So I took the risk. It </span>
  <span id="freeText16541154284293465099" style="display:none"><b>Trigger Warning:</b> <i>a statement at the start of a piece of writing, video, etc., alerting the reader or viewer to the fact that it contains potentially distressing material (often used to introduce a description of such content).</i> Cool huh? Gaiman opens his book of short stories with why he decided on the book’s name, and then states, “What we read as adults should be read, I think, with no warnings or alerts beyond, perhaps: enter at your own risk”.<br /><br />To me, that’s a challenge. So I took the risk. It was worth it. Here are a few of the reasons why:<br /><br /><b>The Thing About Cassandra</b> - This tale would have been good even without the ending that baffled my brain. Flippin’ loved the way Gaiman did that, especially because I did not see it coming. A dozen or so years after high school was left in the past, a friend and Stuart Inne’s mom tell him how they’d each run into Stuart’s first girlfriend. “Who?” asks Stuart. Then we read this line:<br /><i>
  <blockquote>"The thing about Cassandra is this: I’d made her up.”</blockquote>
</i> Made up: yes. Is she somehow real? Could be. That’s all I will say, except to mention that the story will suck you in and spit you out.<br /><b>The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountains</b> - A man’s daughter has been missing for a decade before he seeks the cave that holds treasures of gold. You might ask, as I did, “What does gold have to do with his daughter?” The answer is in the tale and its title. Like many of these stories, this one has an ambiguous beginning. Pieces are subtly added until the full picture is revealed. It reminds me of the building of a jigsaw puzzle without the use of the box as a guide. <br /><b>The Case of Death and Honey</b> - It makes sense that Arthur Conan Doyle would influence Gaiman’s work. He pays homage to Doyle by writing a case that maybe only Sherlock could solve. What’s so interesting is the way it’s put together, in letters and correspondence. Again, I could not figure the direction until near the end which makes the final paragraphs so satisfying.<br /><b>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury</b> - You don’t have to be a Bradbury fan to love it, but it helps. Only a few pages long, and all of it’s good.<br /><b>The Black Dog</b> - I can almost hear the fans of American Gods hooing and haaing because Shadow is back. That’s so cool. In truth I have pretty well forgotten the plot and feel of American Gods, but still, this was a pretty decent short. Another mystery, and is Gaiman once again recalling Sherlock here? He drops a little hint when mentioning The Hound of the Baskervilles. This one comes with some evil and magic.<br /><br />I recommend Trigger Warning to Gaiman fans. If you’re new to his work, then in my opinion <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14497.Neverwhere" title="Neverwhere by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neverwhere</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16793.Stardust" title="Stardust by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Stardust</a> are the better starting point. Trigger Warning is fascinating in the shear vastness of imagination because every story is different. So why the 3 stars (<b>3.5</b> to be exact)? Well, some very good stories (see above + a few others) are mixed with others which were good, but a tad less interesting – to me anyway (note: this does not mean bad).<br /><br />Thank you for reading this review! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16541154284293465099" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1489594815" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9330286514235817425"><b>OMG!</b><br/><br/>So many wonderful and amazing short stories all wrapped up in an amazing book! Seriously! I have no idea how I even came across this book but I'm so happy that I did. I think this is my second book from him that I've read.. it could be my third too.. I have no idea. I just know that I have a bunch of his books on my TBR.<br/><br/><i>Trigger Warning</i> gave you stories from Sherlock Holmes and Doctor Who to some creepy or romantic stories. It gave you a wide variety of stories that you are bound to fall in l</span>
  <span id="freeText9330286514235817425" style="display:none"><b>OMG!</b><br /><br />So many wonderful and amazing short stories all wrapped up in an amazing book! Seriously! I have no idea how I even came across this book but I'm so happy that I did. I think this is my second book from him that I've read.. it could be my third too.. I have no idea. I just know that I have a bunch of his books on my TBR.<br /><br /><i>Trigger Warning</i> gave you stories from Sherlock Holmes and Doctor Who to some creepy or romantic stories. It gave you a wide variety of stories that you are bound to fall in love with at least one of them.<br /><br />I liked a lot of them, like: The Case of Death and Honey mostly because I just love Sherlock Holmes. Anything that has to do with him is obviously awesome and I'll probably end up loving it. Click-Clack the Rattlebag, was a super creepy one that had such good twists in it. It made me cringe (in the good way - if there is one?) and I just ended up loving it. Sometimes you need a good scary story in your life. Thank god it isn't Friday the 13th or Halloween because I'd probably crap my pants. The Sleeper and the Spindle was AHHHMAZZZINGGG. It had strong female characters. It also gave you a bad ass queen to fall in love with. I mean who doesn't love a good fairy tale cross over kind of book. Anything that resembles a disney princess (yes I said that because I grew up with disney!!) is alright in my book.<br /><br />I could go on and on about all of the stories within this amazing book but I wont. WHY? Well, because you people need to go get this book and read it for yourselves! Honestly, it wont take that much time off of your hands. You'll breeze through it and hopefully you'll love it and thank me for it.<br /><br />Seriously, go read it. NOW!<br /><br /></span>

It place the entire tale the old man told in a different light.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Thing About Cassandra</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776590i/28691727._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="4Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>"The Thing about Cassandra is this: I’d made her up"</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579524868i/28810121._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="518" alt="photo booth strip" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>This was bizarre and thought-provoking. What will you do if someone you <i>"made up"</i> come looking for you?<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Down to the Sunless Sea</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576832745i/28640550._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="5Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>"The sea took him."</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579525238i/28810177._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="602" alt="bone" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This was bone-chilling creepy. I literally got shivers down my spine at the crux of the story.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountain</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776590i/28691727._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="4Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>"Everything has its cost"</b><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579588171i/28814543._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="497" alt="cave" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>I would love to see the performance with the string quartet and Eddie Campbell’s art.<br>This is one of those deep stories, where you just keep falling, and falling. And every time you think about it, you can’t help but fall deeper.<br>This Graphic Novel is moving to the top of my Wish list.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>My Last Landlady</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776590i/28691727._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="4Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”but why must they stand so still?”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580817943i/28901855.jpg" width="276" height="183" alt="Brighton" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Gave me the chills when I read the end and release the narrator is talking to the reader.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Adventure Story</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580817943i/28901856._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="1Star" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”any minor disaster we survived”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580817943i/28901857.jpg" width="400" height="96" alt="Adventure" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>To me this felt like a rambling of a mad person, but then again it might be exactly that.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Orange</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580817943i/28901856._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="1Star" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”The weirdest thing was that I could still see it with my eyes closed”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1580817943i/28901858.jpg" width="225" height="225" alt="fail" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>While I appreciate what Gaiman tried to do here, this story delivery just doesn’t work for me.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>A Calendar of Tales</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”Did they tell you that a year would be a lifetime”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581065848i/28918075.jpg" width="225" height="224" alt="calendar" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is a compellation of 12 shorter stories. Each somehow connected to their month. Some I enjoyed more than other.<br>My favorites are February, March and October. (a lost pendant, a Pirate and a Genie)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Case of Death and Honey</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776590i/28691727._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="4Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”I am only alive when I perceive a challenge”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581402573i/28941731.jpg" width="234" height="160" alt="Honey" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I’ve been meaning to read Sherlock Holmes for a while now, but never seem to get around to actually doing it. This dazzling little story just gave me that longing to again move it up on my TBR.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”I am forgetting things, which scares me”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581416371i/28942424.png" width="400" height="130" alt=" Ray Bradbury" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Losing words and concepts is a scary thing. I can’t even imagine how it would feel to look for a word and only find an empty space where it used to be. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Jerusalem</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”It’s still the Holy City”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581427948i/28943733.jpg" width="300" height="168" alt="Jerusalem" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And this is why I read… to learn. I have never heard of Jerusalem syndrome before today.<br>I would have like for this story to be a bit longer… maybe know what his wife will say when he listens this time.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Click-Clack the Rattlebag</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”Mostly they come from the dark”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581589582i/28956811.jpg" width="300" height="168" alt="House" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Creepy; but not really that surprising or shocking. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>An Invocation of Incuriosity</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776590i/28691727._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="4Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”That is the nature of time. It flows faster when it is younger and the course is narrower.”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581589582i/28956810.jpg" width="183" height="275" alt="door" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I love when stories stretch my mind, when it makes me think… <i>”What if…</i><br>And that is exactly what this story did. I seems I love stories with <b>Doors</b>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>‘And Weep, Like Alexander’</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776504i/28691725._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="2Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>I made a list of inventions the world would be better off without and, one by one, I<br>uninvented them all.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1581589582i/28956812.jpg" width="224" height="225" alt="unmaking" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Interesting concept, but I would like a whole novel - Following Obediah around on his adventures of uninventing.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Nothing O’Clock</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”Watch out for masks”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582027210i/28981182._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="597" alt="masks" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Fascinating concept, but I didn’t connect with this story. Don’t know if it is because I never seen a Doctor Who story before, or if it was just not 100% for me.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Diamonds and Pearls: A Fairy Tale</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776504i/28691725._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="2Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”Once upon the olden times”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582793493i/29026098.jpg" width="282" height="179" alt="Fairy Tale" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This doesn’t feel like a story, it feels more like an idea of a story.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Return of the Thin White Duke</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”I wonder if any of us set out to be monsters?”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1582811610i/29027501.jpg" width="183" height="275" alt="Duke " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And that is how Gaiman believe Bowie came to existence. His imagination surly is something different.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Feminine Endings</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463702175i/19148963.png" width="40" height="8" alt="3Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”Too often people will not see what does not move”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583586250i/29069995._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="statue" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is the creepiest love letter I’ve ever read. It gives me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36430011.You__You___1_" title="You (You, #1) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">You</a> vibes.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Observing the formalities</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776504i/28691725._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="2Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”Manners are all, and the formalities. When we lose those We have lost everything.”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583586250i/29069997._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="224" alt="etiquette" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Talk about changing the point of view… This was certainly something different and unexpected. But I can’t say I liked it that much.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>The Sleeper and the Spindle</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776590i/28691727._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="4Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”She’s old as the hills, evil as a snake, all malevolence and magic and death”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583586250i/29069994._SY540_.png" width="400" height="564" alt="Snow&amp;dwarfs" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I do like fairytale retellings, especially with unexpected twist like this. My only complaint is that we never learn why the spiders was not influenced by the sleeping curse.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <u>Witch Work</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776504i/28691725._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="2Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <pre>The witch was as old as the mulberry tree<br>She lived in the house of a hundred clocks</pre>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583586250i/29069996._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="570" alt="vers" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This one kind of confused me…<br>I liked the parts were the focus is on the witch, but the other parts just didn’t work for me.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578900493i/28766316._SX540_.png" width="400" height="100" alt="line" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>b&gt;<u>In Relig Odhráin</u><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1577776504i/28691725._SX540_.png" width="40" height="8" alt="2Stars" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>”God is not what you imagine”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583586250i/29069998.jpg" width="400" height="302" alt="Relig Odhráin &amp; St Oran's Chapel" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This one sure is disturbing, burring people in walls</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1176688232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1176688232" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1689436-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384982097p2/1689436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1176688232?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1689436-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062330291" href="/book/show/22500611-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1689436-amanda?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1176688232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9559180287967456525"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://guninactone.wordpress.com/2015/01/29/review-trigger-warning-short-stories-and-disturbances/'>https://guninactone.wordpress.com/201...</a><br/><br/>I’ll be honest and say that Neil Gaiman could publish his grocery list and I’d read it. American Gods is pretty much my favorite book in the world. I reread it once a year and I always find something new. So I basically stood up and danced around my office when I received an early copy of these short stories. I know I just said last week I don’t really do short stories, but people, it’s Neil Gaiman. I would rather have a full length novel, but I really enj</span>
  <span id="freeText9559180287967456525" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://guninactone.wordpress.com/2015/01/29/review-trigger-warning-short-stories-and-disturbances/">https://guninactone.wordpress.com/201...</a><br /><br />I’ll be honest and say that Neil Gaiman could publish his grocery list and I’d read it. American Gods is pretty much my favorite book in the world. I reread it once a year and I always find something new. So I basically stood up and danced around my office when I received an early copy of these short stories. I know I just said last week I don’t really do short stories, but people, it’s Neil Gaiman. I would rather have a full length novel, but I really enjoyed these overall.<br /><br />To begin, I actually loved the lengthy prologue. Gaiman goes through each story and describes why it was written or who it was written for. I really liked that extra personal touch and I felt it made for richer reading-despite the short format. I loved the female pirate in “A Calendar of Tales” and “The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury” touched my heart. There’s even a story of an igloo built of books-what booklover wouldn’t be drawn to that? “The Sleeper and the Spindle” was a fantastic fairy tale twist and definitely gave me the shivers while I was reading. “Click-Clack the Rattlebag” was deliciously creepy.<br /><br />My issue often times with short story anthologies is the tie-ins to other books or series that I might not have read. Two stories in Trigger Warning reflect two of Gaiman’s own books, American Gods and The Ocean at the End of the Lane. “The Case of Death and Honey” is Gaiman’s Sherlock Holmes story but also with a nod to Laurie King’s Mary Russell and Holmes series. Though that series is still on my lengthy to be read list, I still found that story to be one of my favorites. I’ve never read a Doctor Who book, despite the fact that I’ve been watching the show since I was 3. While I doubt I’ll seek out a full length book, I did still like “Nothing O’clock”, the story featuring the Doctor.<br /><br />In the past when I’ve read short stories I find my mind wandering trying to figure out how much is left-because its not usually enough. The best praise I can give Trigger Warning is to say that I was completely immersed in most of the stories. I was intrigued, entertained and even a bit rattled by Gaiman’s words.<br /><br />4 stars!<br /><br />Thank you William Morrow and Edelweiss for this advance copy in exchange for an honest opinion!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9559180287967456525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

There are a few poems scattered throughout - most of them are at least fleetingly enjoyable, regardless how you might otherwise feel about poetry.   <span id="freeText6084487409958471170" style="display:none">Gaiman admits his short stories and poems are his opportunity to experiment as a writer. There are a few poems scattered throughout - most of them are at least fleetingly enjoyable, regardless how you might otherwise feel about poetry. The American Gods story at the end is worth reading for Shadow Moon fans. <br /><br />- The Chair (poem) - 3/5 - you have to love an author who can make an amusing poem of out the assembling of an office chair<br />- A Lunar Labyrinth - 2/5 - might like it better if I got the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/23069.Gene_Wolfe" title="Gene Wolfe" rel="nofollow noopener">Gene Wolfe</a> references<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23692654.The_Thing_About_Cassandra" title="The Thing About Cassandra by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thing About Cassandra</a> - 3/5 - imaginary girlfriend in Canada? never know what they get up to when unsupervised<br />- Orange - 4/5 - best set of deposition answers I've ever read<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17404588.A_Calendar_of_Tales" title="A Calendar of Tales by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">A Calendar of Tales</a> - 4/5 - 12 separate tales, each based on a different month of the year<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21632307.The_Case_of_Death_and_Honey" title="The Case of Death and Honey by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Case of Death and Honey</a> - 4/5 - putting the "Bee" in 221 B Baker Street<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15713378.The_Man_Who_Forgot_Ray_Bradbury" title="The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Man Who Forgot Ray Bradbury</a> - 3/5 - Gaiman's love letter to Bradbury<br />- Jerusalem - 3/5 - informed by the author's visit to the Holy City<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16109478.Click_Clack_the_Rattlebag" title="Click-Clack the Rattlebag by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Click-Clack the Rattlebag</a> - 4/5 - Moral of the story: never agree to babysit your girlfriend's little brother<br />- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23692649.An_Invocation_of_Incuriosity" title="An Invocation of Incuriosity by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">An Invocation of Incuriosity</a> - 4/5 - Jack Vance would be proud<br />- "And Weep, Like Alexander" - 4/5 - fun little homage to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7779.Arthur_C__Clarke" title="Arthur C.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=anthological-astuteness">anthological-astuteness</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer10793982184801810275">Actual rating 3.5 stars.<br/><br/>Gaiman is undoubtedly a master of the art of writing: his prose his sublime, his imagery evocative and his characters raw and real. His writing alone is worthy of garnering all five stars. The subject matters were also of a varied and intriguing nature that aroused my initial interest. As the title describes, each story deals with themes that could be deemed as triggers, or unsuitable for those of a sensitive nature, and this both excited and charmed my morbid curiosity a</span>
  <span id="freeText10793982184801810275" style="display:none">Actual rating 3.5 stars.<br /><br />Gaiman is undoubtedly a master of the art of writing: his prose his sublime, his imagery evocative and his characters raw and real. His writing alone is worthy of garnering all five stars. The subject matters were also of a varied and intriguing nature that aroused my initial interest. As the title describes, each story deals with themes that could be deemed as triggers, or unsuitable for those of a sensitive nature, and this both excited and charmed my morbid curiosity and I.<br /><br />My only problem with this is that it features short fiction. It seems unfair to rate a short story collection lowly precisely because it is what it says it is! I just couldn't get over the format enough to fully immerse myself in each story as much as I would have liked to. Gaiman's bizarre and beautiful prose is, in my belief, better suited to longer fiction. My opinion was reinforced by my enjoyment of the longer length stories in this collection. This is just a personal preference has in no way impacted my enjoyment of Gaiman's writing or my interest in reading more of his unusual and astounding creations.</span>

<div id="review_1198572222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198572222" />
    <a title="Rikke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4327582-rikke"><img alt="Rikke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594580741p2/4327582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198572222?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rikke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rikke" href="/user/show/4327582-rikke">Rikke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781472217684" href="/book/show/23628916-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198572222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18408564356342030793">Beautifully sinister. Filled with irresistible darkness. Neil Gaiman is a writer of fantastic fiction, and 'Trigger Warning' is fantastic.<br/><br/>Some of the fragments in here bids me welcome from the past. "The Sleeper and the Spindle" is a sensational masterpiece, I read multiple times last year, living in the fairy tale while it lasted. "A Calendar of Tales" is as beautiful as it is haunting, and the story behind the little stories is mesmerizing. The idea of writing an entire story based on a single</span>
  <span id="freeText18408564356342030793" style="display:none">Beautifully sinister. Filled with irresistible darkness. Neil Gaiman is a writer of fantastic fiction, and 'Trigger Warning' is fantastic.<br /><br />Some of the fragments in here bids me welcome from the past. "The Sleeper and the Spindle" is a sensational masterpiece, I read multiple times last year, living in the fairy tale while it lasted. "A Calendar of Tales" is as beautiful as it is haunting, and the story behind the little stories is mesmerizing. The idea of writing an entire story based on a single sentence from a stranger is complex and rich, ultimately suggesting that inspiration can come from the most unlikely sources.<br /><br />Some of the fragments in here were surprises. Things I did not expect to find within a collection of Neil Gaiman-stories. As someone who has never watched a single episode of 'Doctor Who', I was not prepared to read a story about the TV-show. But I did, as Neil Gaiman had written it, and I enjoyed it more than I ever thought possible. It didn't matter that I didn't have a firm grip on the structures within the Whovian-world, what mattered was Gaiman's words, and they told me everything that I needed to know.<br />Neither did I expect to read a crime-story by Neil Gaiman. Even if it was based on Sherlock Holmes, it came as a pleasant surprise. Elegant, well-crafted and mysterious; classic Sherlock Holmes blended with Gaiman's trademark mystery. <br /><br />And, of course, some of the fragments in here were classic Gaiman-productions. Something you'd expect a true magician to write with ink of liquid beauty. "Feminine Endings" is brutally claustrophobic, a stalker circling in on his victim, manipulating words to express caressing love while speaking of a violent obsession. "The Truth is a Cave in the Black Mountains" was equally drawing, made up of vivid imagery and told as a fairytale-esque myth. Exactly as original, beautiful and disturbing as one would expect. <br /><br />"Trigger Warning" is a wonderful story collection, filled with monsters, things and words that will creep under your skin and stay there. Gaiman's stories are triggers, and do consider yourself warned. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18408564356342030793" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1193299050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1193299050" />
    <a title="Edafe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5668214-edafe"><img alt="Edafe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592133650p2/5668214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1193299050?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edafe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edafe" href="/user/show/5668214-edafe">Edafe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1193299050" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16181629131274738762">Neil Gaiman is a bastard. A beautifully talented writer and an absolute bastard for getting into my head and rooting about. Right from the start I got the chills and I hadn't even reached the stories, this was just the introduction. I know I'm loving a book, a song, a film, any piece of work because it short circuits my logical brain and sneaks in. I feel tingles. When Neil describes his love for short stories, his journey to writing this compilation, it hit like a whirlpool: strong and unexpect</span>
  <span id="freeText16181629131274738762" style="display:none">Neil Gaiman is a bastard. A beautifully talented writer and an absolute bastard for getting into my head and rooting about. Right from the start I got the chills and I hadn't even reached the stories, this was just the introduction. I know I'm loving a book, a song, a film, any piece of work because it short circuits my logical brain and sneaks in. I feel tingles. When Neil describes his love for short stories, his journey to writing this compilation, it hit like a whirlpool: strong and unexpected. <br /><br />After kicking up emotional debris, I had to put it down and have a cup of tea. I collected myself, then I started to read. I can't say I loved every story, that would be a lie and this book deserves Truth. The truth is, some were hard going, one was dull, one made me ache a little for my Doctor but all made me think. Each story got my brain revving and pinging with painful, delightful ideas, thoughts and a touch of wistfulness. <br /><br />I posited once that "Reading is the closest thing to sharing a stream of consciousness; to being inside someone’s head without barriers" and writing like this means "someone somewhere can share my soul, just for the briefest of moments".</span>
  <a data-text-id="16181629131274738762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1175761875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175761875" />
    <a title="Bob/Sally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally"><img alt="Bob/Sally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598307870p2/2224905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175761875?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob/Sally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob/Sally" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally">Bob/Sally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062330291" href="/book/show/22500611-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175761875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6410082092325988981"><i>Disclaimer: I received an ARC of this title from the author or publisher in exchange for review consideration. While I make every attempt to avoid spoilers, please be aware that details provided in an ARC synopsis, press release, or review request that I've assumed common knowledge may differ from the final published cover blurb.</i><br/><br/><br/>With his third collection of short fiction, Neil Gaiman presents us with stories, verse, and even a 50th anniversary Doctor Who story, all previously published (please n</span>
  <span id="freeText6410082092325988981" style="display:none"><i>Disclaimer: I received an ARC of this title from the author or publisher in exchange for review consideration. While I make every attempt to avoid spoilers, please be aware that details provided in an ARC synopsis, press release, or review request that I've assumed common knowledge may differ from the final published cover blurb.</i><br /><br /><br />With his third collection of short fiction, Neil Gaiman presents us with stories, verse, and even a 50th anniversary Doctor Who story, all previously published (please note that Black Dog, the one story exclusive to the collection, was not included in the ARC).<br /><br />Having only read him in novel or graphic novel form, Trigger Warning: Short Fictions and Disturbances was my first introduction to Gaiman's short fiction. It was an interesting read, largely entertaining, and even if there was a long, deep stretch of works in the middle that just didn't grab my attention, there were more than enough strong entries to book-end that gap.<br /><br />Rather than review every tale in the collection, I thought I'd just offer my observations on those that worked best for me:<br /><br /><i>The Thing About Cassandra</i> was most definitely an early highlight, and even if I saw the twist coming a few pages early, it was still a great story.<br /><br /><i>Down to a Sunless Sea</i> was one of the shorter tales here, but powerful in the depths of its sorrow. <i>The Truth Is a Cave in the Black Mountains . . .</i> was absolutely fantastic, with the stunning image of a girl perhaps too-tightly bound by her ponytail, and marked by the cleverness of a promise. <i>Adventure Story</i> was too short, but unexpectedly comic, while <i>Orange</i> was odd, oddly told, and oddly compelling.<br /><br /><i>Click-­Clack the Rattlebag</i> was really just a tease, ending just as we get to the meat of it, but I quite liked the monstrous concepts of the Click-Clack and the Rattlebag. <i>An Invocation of Incuriosity</i> was a great story within a story, full of myth and fable, while <i>“And Weep, Like Alexander”</i> was a fun story about un-inventing and the unintended consequences of progress. <i>Nothing O’Clock</i>, the Doctor Who story, was one of my favorites, taking as its inspiration the simple question of "What time is it, Mr. Wolf?" and making of it something perfectly creepy, properly Who-amusing, and entirely unsettling in its resolution.<br /><br /><i>Pearls: A Fairy Tale</i> was just that - a faery tale - but a contemporary one of drugs, dogs, hookers, stepmothers, and magic, that I quite enjoyed. <i>Kether to Malkuth</i> and <i>The Sleeper and the Spindle</i> both continued the classic faery tale theme, but in a more familiar setting . . . even if Gaiman puts a few unexpected twists on the traditional tropes.<br /><br />Introductions are always a tricky thing when it comes to a collection, and you wonder/worry about how much the author might give away, but I think it fits here as an intro (rather than an appendix). Gaiman really sets the stage for each tale, telling us less about them and more about how they came about. They allowed me to appreciate some stories (such as <i>A Calendar of Tales</i>), even if I didn't enjoy them, and really served to expose his inspirations. All in all, Trigger Warning: Short Fictions and Disturbances is a solid collection, despite the dry spot in the center, and perfect for those of who don't follow his short fiction obsessively.<br /><br /><br /><i>Originally reviewed at <a href="http://beauty-in-ruins.blogspot.ca/2015/01/fiction-review-trigger-warning-by-neil.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty in Ruins</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6410082092325988981" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1170603848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170603848" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1170603848?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1170603848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12917270755789387892">I discovered Neil Gaiman as a teen, thanks to the Science Fiction Book Club. The selection of the month one month was GOOD OMENS, by Gaiman and Terry Pratchett, and their glowing and hilarious review made me order it immediately. It didn't disappoint, and remains one of my favorite books. Then I found STARDUST. Different, strange, but still wonderful. The next thing I read was SMOKE & MIRRORS, and there my growing love for Neil Gaiman ran into a bit of a hitch. I didn't like most of the stories.</span>
  <span id="freeText12917270755789387892" style="display:none">I discovered Neil Gaiman as a teen, thanks to the Science Fiction Book Club. The selection of the month one month was GOOD OMENS, by Gaiman and Terry Pratchett, and their glowing and hilarious review made me order it immediately. It didn't disappoint, and remains one of my favorite books. Then I found STARDUST. Different, strange, but still wonderful. The next thing I read was SMOKE &amp; MIRRORS, and there my growing love for Neil Gaiman ran into a bit of a hitch. I didn't like most of the stories. And I realized, then and now, that I was probably too young for them. I remember being disturbed by a couple of the stories for years. I still have my copy, but I've never opened the book again. And for a while I felt like maybe there was something wrong with me. Like maybe I was too immature, and now as an adult, am I being an old fuddy-duddy for not thinking they are all genius and racing to reread them? But no. I contend that I'm not. It's interesting, because we are so caught up, as parents, as a reading culture, in urging more and more advanced books on readers, because they can handle the vocabulary, because it's important that kids know that Things Happen. Death. Divorce. Violence. Drugs. But I think we fail to see that you can tell a kid the nuts and bolts of sex or violence, but reading about it in fiction is still going to be rough for them, that emotionally they weren't ready. And I like to think, having read this, that Neil Gaiman would actually agree with me.<br /><br />So the title of this collection is TRIGGER WARNING. And he talks in the introduction (which is wonderful) about why it's called that. And he mentions that growing up he read a lot of books that were beyond him, and some he just didn't understand, and some he wished he hadn't read. And I thought Yes. See. I have things I wish I hadn't read. Or that I had read later in my life, which is the case with SMOKE AND MIRRORS.<br /><br />But is not the case here. <br /><br />Now that my digression about emotional maturity and books is done, I can tell you: I loved this collection. I think this was overall his strongest collection of stories. Usually anthologies are a mixed bag, and one or two at the very least is awful, and/or forgettable. But there isn't a bum story in the bunch. Every one is a shining gem, a delight to behold, and I loved them all. What shocked me about his earlier collection, and continued on in FRAGILE THINGS as well, was that so many of the stories were just . . . grim. STARDUST and NEVERWHERE get pretty dark, yet I still think of them as having a playful tone overall. I see them as being written with love, and a certain sense of whimsy that is lacking in so many of Gaiman's shorter pieces. Even in ANANSI BOYS, which gets darkity-dark-dark, there's the whole bit about Fat Charlie and the lime. So what pleased me about these new stories is that the sense of playfulness was back. Some of the stories were freakin' creepy, but the memory of them still makes me smile, if that makes sense. <br /><br />If you're looking to discover Neil Gaiman, you could do worse than read this. I would also recommend his M IS FOR MAGIC, which contains his stories suitable for children, including my two favorites, "Chivalry" and "Sunbird." Also, if you are a fan of AMERICAN GODS, which I most assuredly am, the last story is a novella about Shadow, which made me endlessly happy. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12917270755789387892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5048433501127530007">Some pieces were better than others, but that is par for the course in a book of short pieces, even when you are Neil Gaiman. That being said, I really enjoyed much of the material in this collection. There were many times when I raced along, breathlessly turning pages and wishing the book would not end. It showcases the wide range of tone, style and genre of which Gaiman is capable. There is tragedy, comedy, satire, pathos, legend, folklore, horror and poetry. One other feature I enjoyed was th</span>
  <span id="freeText5048433501127530007" style="display:none">Some pieces were better than others, but that is par for the course in a book of short pieces, even when you are Neil Gaiman. That being said, I really enjoyed much of the material in this collection. There were many times when I raced along, breathlessly turning pages and wishing the book would not end. It showcases the wide range of tone, style and genre of which Gaiman is capable. There is tragedy, comedy, satire, pathos, legend, folklore, horror and poetry. One other feature I enjoyed was the introduction, in which the author takes the time to give a little information on how each piece came to be; he is also humble enough to acknowledge other writers who influenced and inspired him.</span>

<div id="review_1211257356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211257356" />
    <a title="Milica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5107980-milica"><img alt="Milica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592069237p2/5107980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1211257356?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Milica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Milica" href="/user/show/5107980-milica">Milica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781472217691" href="/book/show/24486629-trigger-warning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5107980-milica?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211257356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12790952197082098760">Ne postoji zbirka kratkih priča u kojoj je svaka priča odlična, bar se ja nisam susrela sa takvom još uvek. Prednost kratkih priča u odnosu na romane, je što nije neophodno da vam se svaka priča dopadne da biste na kraju knjige bili oduševljeni. Ukoliko vam pisac "ne pogodi žicu" u romanu nema izlaza. U zbirkama, ako vam se neka priča ne svidi tu je neka druga,treća,peta... I za svačiji ukus i raspoloženje će se naći nešto (osim ako ste potpuno promašili žanr ili uopšte nemate ukusa u tom slučaj</span>
  <span id="freeText12790952197082098760" style="display:none">Ne postoji zbirka kratkih priča u kojoj je svaka priča odlična, bar se ja nisam susrela sa takvom još uvek. Prednost kratkih priča u odnosu na romane, je što nije neophodno da vam se svaka priča dopadne da biste na kraju knjige bili oduševljeni. Ukoliko vam pisac "ne pogodi žicu" u romanu nema izlaza. U zbirkama, ako vam se neka priča ne svidi tu je neka druga,treća,peta... I za svačiji ukus i raspoloženje će se naći nešto (osim ako ste potpuno promašili žanr ili uopšte nemate ukusa u tom slučaju vam nema pomoći).<br /><br />Treća zbirka Nila Gejmena (treća za "odraslu" publiku) se sastoji od 24 priče i veoma informativnog uvoda. Sastoji se dugih priča i od veoma kratkih pričica. Nisu mi sve bile po ukusu i samima im ne bih dala visoku ocenu, ali one druge...Oh, one druge! Jezovite, maštovite, duhovite i tako gejmenovske u onom čudnom, gotovo bizarnom stilu.<br /><br />Smatram da nije neophodno da svaku priču ponaosob ocenjujem, ali istaćiću par omiljenih:<br /><br />* " Lunar Labyrinth"<br />* "Click-Clack the Rattlebag" <br />* "The Sleeper and the Spindle"<br />* "Down to a Sunless Sea"<br />* "Nothing o'clock"<br /><br />"FINAL WARNING There are monsters in these pages, but as Ogden Nash pointed out in my first short-story collection, Smoke and Mirrors, where there’s a monster, there’s also a miracle. There are some long stories and some short ones. There are a handful of poems, which perhaps might need their own warning for the people who are frightened, disturbed, or terminally puzzled by poetry. (In my second short-story collection, Fragile Things, I tried to explain that the poems come free. They are bonuses for the kind of people who do not need to worry about sneaky and occasional poems lurking inside their short-story collections.) There. Consider yourself warned. There are so many little triggers out there, being squeezed in the darkness even as I write this. This book is correctly labeled. Now all we have to worry about is all the other books, and, of course, life, which is huge and complicated and will not warn you before it hurts you. Thank you for coming. Enjoy the things that never happened. Secure your own mask again after you read these stories, but do not forget to help others.” </span>
  <a data-text-id="12790952197082098760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ACrvXk1TylA7pZjLy/Uly+gLdIJ7hyoypzy1hRWEd2l9eaJHeCTI9ADxIyjHQIJMaiqw3PCrBayWXUHuVA1JTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rgMAeTzK5DrHG0FLWa2YqWZ1vkrJKFYr20vycmehfQ3TUE1gCb3mnvxP+qhVGD8u5FR6FEIEebXqKgYZJihDKg==')})
  }
//]]>

Beginning with his debut play, The Zoo Story (1958), and on to his barrier breaking works of the 1960s, most notably The American Dream (1960), Who\'s Afraid of Virginia Woolf? (1963), and the Pulitzer Prize-winning A Delicate Balance (1966), Albee\'s unsparing indictment of the American way of life earned him early distinction as the dramatist of his generation. His acclaim was enhanced further in the decades that followed with prize-winning dramas such as Seascape (1974) and Three Tall Women (1991), as well as recent works like The Play About the Baby (2001) and The Goat. (2002). Albee has brought the same critical force to his non-theatrical prose. Stretching My Mind collects for the first time ever the author\'s writings on theater, literature, and the political and cultural battlegrounds that have defined his career. Many of the selections were drawn from Albee\'s private papers, and almost all previously published material--dating from 1960 to the present--has never been reprinted.
